Jamison Brereton

45 (486)
Indra
┼Ъaс╣Гyu B─Бrhaspatya
33 verses: g─Бyatr─л, except atinicrt 29, anu ╠е с╣гс╣нubh 33, arranged in trcas ╠е
Like the preceding hymn, this one is composed of tr╠еcas, the first ten to Indra, the last one (vss. 31тАУ33) a d─Бnastuti to the patron Br╠еbu. Given its position in the Indra cycle, it is unlikely to have been originally a single hymn, but there are some themes that keep recurring throughout the hymn, such as the comparison of Indra with a cow or calf (vss. 7, 22, 25тАУ26, 28), the sacred formulation as a vehicle for Indra (vss. 4, 7, 19), and the stake that is set as a prize in a contest (vss. 2, 11тАУ13, 15). However, rhetorical unity within tr╠еcas seems almost entirely lacking.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Indra This hymn contains 5 instances of the phrase тАЬthe stake (that is) set,тАЭ hit├бdh├бna-: 3 acc. sg. hit├бс╣Г dh├бnam (2c, 12c, 15c), 2 loc. sg. (11b, 13b). All but one of these has the order just given, but one of the loc. exx. (13b) is found in the opposite order, as dh├бne hit├й as opposed to 11b hit├й dh├бne, which matches the order of the accusatives. A survey of the other examples of the phrase in the RV turns up one more ex. of the acc. hit├бс╣Г dh├бnam (VIII.80.8), but a number of further loc. exx., almost all of which have the flipped order found in 13b dh├бne hit├й (I.40.2=VI.61.5, I.116.15, I.132.5, VIII.3.9, IX.53.2) versus hit├й dh├бne (X.63.14). There is only one ex. of the phrase outside of the acc. sg. and loc. sg., namely dh├бneс╣гu hit├йс╣гu (VIII.16.5). It thus appears that the acc. and loc. exx. have different underlying orders. Since the word order in this phrase, in both acc. and loc., is, at least to the naked eye, metrically indifferent (always тПС - тПС -), it is hard to see what is driving the variable order, esp. since almost all instantiations of this phrase are p─Бda-final (except for I.116.15 and 132.5). Within this very limited data set, it would be possible to assume that the variant order signals different syntactic intentions: тАЬthe set stakeтАЭ (acc.) as opposed to the loc. absol. тАЬwhen the stake (is/was) set,тАЭ with secondary predication. Dieter Gunkel (pers. comm.) tells me that he produced a similar (independent) hypothesis when investigating тАЬswappable bigramsтАЭ with Kevin Ryan (some of which results were presented in Vienna, June 24, 2015).

However, given the vagaries of RVic word order, it is difficult to know if such a hypothesis would hold up across a large set of data. It would be useful to investigate word order in clear loc. absolutes.

English translation:

тАЬMay that youthful Indra, who, by good guidance, brought Turva┼Ыa and Yadu from afar, (be) our friend.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Who with good leading led Turva┼Ыa and Yadu here from afar,
he is Indra, our youthful comrade.

Griffith

THAT Indra is our youthful Friend, who with his trusty guidance led
Turvasa, Yadu from afar.

Geldner

Der den Turvasa, den Yadu durch gl├╝ckliche F├╝hrung aus der Ferne herf├╝hrte, dieser Indra ist unser jugendlicher Freund.

Der aus der Ferne hergef├╝hrt sch├╢nleitend Jadu, Turva├зa, Der junge Indra ist uns Freund.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIndra gives sustenance, even to the undevout he is the conqueror of wealh accusative ulated (by enemies) though (going against) them with a slow-paced steed.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Placing vitality even in the uninspired, even with a steed lacking speed, Indra is the winner of the stake that is set.

Griffith

Even to the dull and uninspired Indra, gives vital power, and wins
Even with slow steed the offered prize.

Geldner

Auch dem Unberedten verleiht er Schwung, auch mit dem langsamen Rennpferd gewinnt Indra den ausgesetzten Preis.

Grassmann

Auch in den Matten legt er Kraft, mit tr├дgem Rosse auch erlangt Indra den ausgesetzten Preis.

English translation:

тАЬVast are his designs, manifold are his praises, his protections are never withdrawn.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Great is his guidance and many are the encomia for him.
His help does not perish.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I have silently suppressed the plurals in pr├бс╣З─лtayaс╕е and ┼лt├бyaс╕е (guidance and help, rather than guidances and helps). Given that pr├бс╣З─лtayaс╕е reprises ─Б╠Бnayat тАж s├║n─лt─л in the 1st vs. of the tс╣Ыca, it might be better to translate it as тАЬGreat is his leading.тАЭ The three -ti-stem abstracts pr├бс╣З─лti-, pr├б┼Ыasti-, and ┼лt├н- recall s├║n─лti- in 1b.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬOffer worship and praises, friends, to him who is to be attracted by prayers; for he verily is our great intelligence.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Comrades, chant and sing forth to him whose vehicle is the sacred formulation,
for he is great solicitude for us.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As was implied in the published translation, there is more cohesion across tс╣Ыcas than within them. In this 1st vs. of the 2nd tс╣Ыca there are a number of connections to the previous one: the 1st word s├бkh─Бyaс╕е recalls s├бkh─Б in 1c; in b the impv. pr├б тАж g─Бyata тАЬsing forthтАЭ is a variant of the nominal form pr├б┼Ыasti- (3b) to the lexeme pr├б тИЪ┼Ыaс╣Гs тАШproclaim forthтАЩ; in c the nominal clause s├б h├н naс╕е X resembles 1c тАж s├б naс╕е X; c contains another -ti-stem abstract, pr├бmati-, like those in 3 (two of which are cmpded with pr├б-); and the final word of the vs., mah─л╠Б, echoes the 1st word of 3 mah─л╠Бс╕е.

Griffith

Friends, sing your psalm and offer praise to him to whom the prayer is brought:
For our great Providence is he.

Geldner

Ihr Freunde, lobsinget und stimmt das Lied auf ihn an, den die erbauliche Rede anzieht; denn er ist unsere gro├Яe Vorsehung.

Grassmann

O Freunde, dem man Andacht weiht, den preist und hebt zu singen an; Denn er ist unser grosser Schutz.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬSlayer of Vс╣Ыtra, you are the protector of one (adorer), or of two, and of such as we are.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

You, o Vr╠еtra-smasher, are the helper of one, of two,
and for such as we are.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The sequence ├йkasya тАж dv├бyoс╕е тАж / ut├йdс╣Ы┼Ыe y├бth─Б vay├бm тАЬof one, of two and for such as we areтАЭ is a nice example of BehagelтАЩs Law. It also shows variant syntax in a conjoined construction, since the third conjoined member is dative (─л╠Бdс╣Ы┼Ыe), while the first two are gen. (unless dv├бyoс╕е is loc., which seems unlikely). The result, at least in translation, is almost awkward, but the formal switch in case (and number) has semantic consequences, in my opinon. The sequence first presents itself as a purely numerical one (cf. Klein DGRV I.332-33), and we might expect тАЬof one, of two, and *of however many we are.тАЭ But the sg. ─л╠Бdс╣Ы┼Ыe changes the focus from the quantity of the beneficiaries to their quality (тАЬsuch as we,тАЭ in implicit contrast to people outside our circle of lesser value), and the dative emphasizes the benefactive nature of IndraтАЩs actions. GeldnerтАЩs тАЬauch f├╝r einen solchen, wie wir sindтАЭ misses the point, in my view.

Griffith

Thou, Slaughterer of Vrtra, art Guardian and Friend of one and two,
Yea, of a man like one of us.

Geldner

Du Vritrat├╢ter bist der Besch├╝tzer von einem, von zweien, auch f├╝r einen solchen, wie wir sind.

Grassmann

English translation:

тАЬYou remove (far from us) those who hate us; you prosper hose who repeat your praise; bestower of excellent male descendants, you are glorified by manтАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Bestower: suv─лra = ┼Ыobhanai v─лraiс╕е putrapautr─Бdibhir d─Бtavyair upetaс╕е, endowed with or possessed of sons, grandsons, and the like to be given

Jamison Brereton

Only you lead (us) beyond hatreds; you make (us) proclaimers of solemn speech;
and you are called rich in heroes by superior men.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I supply тАШusтАЩ as obj. in both a and b, adapted from 4c and esp. 5c; Geldner supplies тАЬM├дnnerтАЭ (in b), presumably on the basis of nr╠еbhiс╕е in c. Either will work, but тАШusтАЩ seems to provide more continuity.

n├бyasi in a connects across tс╣Ыcas with ─Б╠Бnayat in 1a, and uktha┼Ыaс╣Гs├нnaс╕е in b with pr├б┼Ыastayaс╕е in 3b. In 3b Indra is said to have many pr├б┼Ыasti-, and here the producers of these (pr├б)┼Ыasti- are identified (as us or, with Geldner, men).

Griffith

Beyond men’s hate thou leadest us, and givest cause to sing thy praise:
Good hero art thou called by men.

Geldner

Du f├╝hrst ├╝ber die Anfeindungen hinweg, du machst die M├дnner zu Lobs├дngern. Von den M├дnnern wirst du Meister genannt.

Grassmann

Du f├╝hrst uns durch die Feinde hin und regst zu Lobgesang uns an, Bei M├дnnern heisst du ┬╗starker Held┬л.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬI invoke with hymns Indra, our friends, who is Brahma, who is attracted by prayer and entitled to adoration, to milk him as a cow.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Brahma: brahm─Бс╣Зam = parivс╣Ыс╕Нham, great, mighty

Jamison Brereton

To the formulator whose vehicle is the sacred formulation, to the comrade worthy of verses
do I call with my songs, as to a cow to be milked,

English translation:

тАЬWielder of the thunderbolt, lord of ┼Ъaci, demolish the strong (cities) of men; (battle), unbending (Indra) their devices.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

(Tear) apart even the strongholds of the peoples, o possessor of the stone and lord of power;
tear (apart) their tricks, you who canтАЩt be bowed.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. contains two parallel direct objects (тАЬstrongholdsтАЭ and тАЬtricksтАЭ) in two parallel clauses, which presuppose the same verb. The preverb (v├н) is given at the beginning of p─Бda a, the verb (vс╣Ыh├б) itself at the beginning of the 2nd hemistich; they must be assembled to produce the full lexeme.

English translation:

тАЬVeracious Indra, drinker of the Soma, provider of sustenance, we, desirous of food, invoke such as you are.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Such as you are: tam tv─Б ah┼лmahi, we invoke you (who are) that, or such as has been described in the preceding verses

Jamison Brereton

It is just you, o Indra, you real one, you drinker of soma and lord of prizes,
that we have called upon, seeking fameтАФ

Jamison Brereton Notes

After the opening t├бm u tv─Б, the rest of the hemistich consists only of vocc.

satya somap─Б, ├нndra v─Бj─Бn─Бm pate, with only a single accent among them: ├нndra is accented because itтАЩs initial in its p─Бda, while the gen. pl. v─Бj─Бn─Бm is unaccented because itтАЩs part of a voc. phrase. Note that in the Holland & van Nooten Rig Veda edition ed. v─Бj─Бn─Б╠Бm bears an impossible, final-syllable accent, a typo that should be deleted.

10-11 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

These vss. form a syntactic pair characterized by simple enjambment.

Both vss. begin t├бm u tv─Б, with the iteration of this phrase in 11a still part of the main clause of vs. 10 (and the object of 10c ├бh┼лmahi). The rest of the first hemistich of 11 consists of two rel. clauses, whose predicate (the predicate for both clauses), h├бvyaс╕е, is found at the beginning of c. The rest of c is a separate impv. clause. Although the content of these two vss. is banal in the extreme, the syncopated effect produced by having the syntactic units not conform to metrical units gives it a bit of oomph. The vs. pair is unified by the тАШcallтАЩ motif: 10c ├бh┼лmahi тАШwe have called uponтАЩ, 11c h├бvyaс╕е тАШto be called uponтАЩ / h├бvam тАШcallтАЩ. The root тИЪ┼Ыru also provides unity: 10c ┼Ыravasy├бvaс╕е тАШseeking fameтАЩ, 11c ┼Ыrudh─л тАШhearтАЩ, also, in 12b ┼Ыrav─Б╠Бyy─Бn тАШworthy of fameтАЩ.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(We invoke) you, such as you are, you who have been invocable of old, and who are now to be invoked for the wealth held (by the foe); hear our invocation.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Just you, who were before or who are now to be called upon when the stake is set.
Hear our call!

Jamison Brereton Notes

It is worth noting that in the temporally contrastive rel. clauses (a: pur─Б╠Б тАШpreviouslyтАЩ, b: n┼лn├бm тАШnowтАЩ) whose joint predicate is the grdv. h├бvyaс╕е (see above), the one with past reference has an overt copula, pf. ─Б╠Бsitha, while the one with current reference has the copula gapped.

10-11 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

These vss. form a syntactic pair characterized by simple enjambment.

Both vss. begin t├бm u tv─Б, with the iteration of this phrase in 11a still part of the main clause of vs. 10 (and the object of 10c ├бh┼лmahi). The rest of the first hemistich of 11 consists of two rel. clauses, whose predicate (the predicate for both clauses), h├бvyaс╕е, is found at the beginning of c. The rest of c is a separate impv. clause. Although the content of these two vss. is banal in the extreme, the syncopated effect produced by having the syntactic units not conform to metrical units gives it a bit of oomph. The vs. pair is unified by the тАШcallтАЩ motif: 10c ├бh┼лmahi тАШwe have called uponтАЩ, 11c h├бvyaс╕е тАШto be called uponтАЩ / h├бvam тАШcallтАЩ. The root тИЪ┼Ыru also provides unity: 10c ┼Ыravasy├бvaс╕е тАШseeking fameтАЩ, 11c ┼Ыrudh─л тАШhearтАЩ, also, in 12b ┼Ыrav─Б╠Бyy─Бn тАШworthy of fameтАЩ.

Griffith

Such as thou wast of old, and art now to be called on when the prize
lies ready, listen to our call.

рд╕рд╛рдпрдг-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрдореН

рд╣реЗ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рдзреАрднрд┐рдГ рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐рднрд┐рд╕реНрддреНрд╡рджреНрд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрд╛рднрд┐рдГ рдкреНрд░реАрддреЗрди рддреНрд╡рдпрд╛ рдЕрдиреБрдЧреГрд╣реАрддрд╛ рд╡рдпрдореН рдЕрд░реНрд╡рджреНрднрд┐рдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдорджреАрдпреИрдГ рдЕрд╢реНрд╡реИрдГ рдЕрд░реНрд╡рддрдГ рд╢рддреНрд░реБрд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзрд┐рдиреЛрд╜рд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рд╢реНрд░рд╡рд╛рдпреНрдпрд╛рдиреН рд╢реНрд░рд╡рдгреАрдпрд╛рдиреН рдкреНрд░рд╢рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдиреН рд╡рд╛рдЬрд╛рдиреН рдЕрдиреНрдирд╛рдирд┐ рдЪ рд╣рд┐рддрдВ рд╢рддреНрд░реБрд╖реБ рдирд┐рд╣рд┐рддрдВ рдзрдирдВ рдЪ рдЬреЗрд╖реНрдо рддреНрд╡рджрдиреБрдЧреНрд░рд╣рд╛рдЬреНрдЬрдпреЗрдо рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(Favoured) by you, Indra, (who are propitiated), by our hymns, (we ovecome) with our steeds the steeds (of the enemy), and we conquer abundant food, and the wealth held (by the foes).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Literally, with praises, by horses, horses food, excellent Indra by you, we conquer deposited wealth

Jamison Brereton

With insights as our steeds, (might we win) steeds and prizes worthy of fame, o Indra;
with you might we win the stake that is set.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The phrase hit├б- dh├бna- is repeated from 11b and also picks up the same phrase in 2c. (See disc. above.) In fact 12c tv├бy─Б jeс╣гma hit├бс╣Г dh├бnam is a telling variant on 2c ├нndro j├йt─Б hit├бс╣Г dh├бnam. In vs. 2 Indra is described as a/the (habitual) winner of the stake, while by vs. 12 it is we who hope to be the winners with his help. The vocalism of the precative jeс╣гma matches that of the agent noun j├йt─Б in 2.

See further 15c. Note also that 2b contains an instr. ├бrvat─Б тАЬwith a steedтАЭ (in that case an unsatisfactory one) like ├бrvadbhiс╕е in 12a.

The opening of the vs. is called тАЬstark elliptischтАЭ by Geldner, who sees two different possible constructions (n. 12a): тАЬwith insights (might we overcome) (the insights of other poets) and with steeds (might we overcome) steedsтАЭ or тАЬwith insights (as) steeds тАжтАЭ His tr. seems to reflect the first (though without supplying any further material), while I prefer the second.

Griffith

With hymns and coursers we will gain, Indra, through thee, both steeds and spoil
Most glorious, and the proffered prize.

Geldner

Mit weisen Gedanken, mit Rennpferden wollen wir die Rennpferde besiegen, zu Ruhm gereichende Gewinne, o Indra, durch dich den ausgesetzten Kampfpreis ersiegen.

Grassmann

Durch Rosse, Indra, und Gebet lass uns den ausgesetzten Preis Erringen Rosse, Nahrung, Schatz.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬHeroic and adorable Indra, verily you are mighty in battle, and victor of the wealth held (by the enemy).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

You became great when the stake was set, o Indra, you hero who longs for songs,
and the one worth tussling for at the raid.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The new tс╣Ыca opens with yet another example of the тАШstakeтАЩ phrase, this time in opposite order (dh├бne hit├й). For further on the order in this phrase, see the above introduction. comm. to the hymn.

Thou, Indra, Lover of the Song, whom men must stir to help, hast been
Great in the contest for the prize.

Your help that has the quickest speed, o smasher of foesтАФ

English translation:

тАЬVictorious Indra, who are the chief off charioteers, conquer the wealth that is held (by the enemy) with our assailing car.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

As the best charioteer, with our chariot on the attack,
win, o winner, the stake that is set.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The VP тИЪji hit├бс╣Г dh├бnam returns from 2c and 12c, with two instances of тИЪji: j├йс╣гi jiс╣гс╣Зo hit├бс╣Г dh├бnam. Here the subject is Indra as in 2c, not тАШweтАЩ (12c), but he is making use of our (asm─Б╠Бkena) chariot.

Griffith

As skilfullest of those who drive the chariot, with our art and aim,
O Conqueror, win the proffered prize.

Geldner

Als bester Wagenlenker sollst du mit unserem angreifenden Wagen den ausgesetzten Kampfpreis ersiegen, du Siegreicher!

Grassmann

Erringe denn des Kampfes Preis siegreicher, bester Lenker du, Durch unsern Wagen zum Gewinn.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬPraise that Indra who alone has been born the supervisor (of all), the lord of men, the giver of rain.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Praise only him, who alone was born as the limitless lord of the separate peoples,
having a bullish will.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As Oldenberg notes (though not in those terms), we seem to have an embedded main clause here – in that t├бm u stuhi forming the second part of p─Бda a interrupts the rel. cl. that begins the vs. (y├б ├йka ├нd) and continues through the rest of b and c, with the accented verb jaj├▒├й in c. Since y├б ├йka ├нd is in fact only a single constituent, it might be best to consider it fronted around the brief main cl.

Griffith

Praise him who, Matchless and Alone, was born the Lord of living men,
Most active, with heroic soul.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬLord of cattle, (coming) with your mares, saisfy our desires completely with (abundant) food, with horses, and with kine.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

(Coming) here with your teams, fulfill our desire with prizes of horses and of cows, lord of cows, acting boldly.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner takes niy├║dbhiс╕е and v─Б╠Бjebhiс╕е as parallel, and therefore the тАШteamsтАЩ are among the things with which Indra fulfills our desire. Given the position of niy├║dbhiс╕е in the 1st p─Бda and its usual usage, I think it rather refers to IndraтАЩs teams, with which he travels тАШhereтАЩ, and I take ─Б╠Бboth with pс╣Ыс╣Зa and with a verb of motion to be supplied. For a similar use, see VI.22.11 s├б no niy├║dbhiс╕е тАж ─Б╠Бgahi тАж, also addressed to Indra in this cycle.

Griffith

So with thy yoked teams satisfy our wish with power and wealth in steeds
And cattle, boldly, Lord of kine!
22 Sing this, what time the ’ juice is pressed, to him your Hero, Much-invoked,
To please him as a mighty Steer.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬSing praises, when your libation is poured out, to him who is the invoked of many, the subduer (of foes), giving him gratification, like (fresh pasture) to cattle.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Sing this at the pressing to the warrior called upon by many, (this) that is weal for the able one as if for a cow.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The first p─Бda contains the common locution in which a poet addresses himself in the sg., but makes a nod to his ritual colleagues in the 2nd pl.: t├бd vo g─Бya.

Lit. this should be тАЬSing (o poet=me) this, (on behalf of) you all (=priests).тАЭ See my тАЬPoetic Self-Reference in the Rig Veda and the Persona of ZarathustraтАЭ (Fs.

Skjaerv├╕, BAI 19 [2005]), where this passage is disc. p. 69. The effort to introduce the 2nd pl. into the English would overbalance the tr., in a way that the slender enclitic vaс╕е does not.

The simile in c is somewhat unsettling: тАЬSing what is weal for the able one as if for a cow.тАЭ Presumably itтАЩs not the song that would be weal for a/the cow. S─Бyaс╣Зa.тАЩs explan., reported by Geldner (n. 22c), may well be correct: тАЬas (fodder is) for a cow.тАЭ Recall also 7c g─Б╠Бс╣Г n├б d├│hase huve тАЬI call upon (Indra) like a cow for milking,тАЭ where the cow simile is filled out. In light of this passage it may be that here what is weal for the cow is not fodder but rather the call to be milked, which would better resemble the song that is weal for Indra: тАЬSing what is weal for the able one, as (a milking call) is for a cow.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton Notes

This tс╣Ыca concerns itself with cows, picking up g├│madbhir gopate from the end of the preceding tс╣Ыca (21c). In particular 23b v─Б╠Бjasya g├│mataс╕е тАЬprize of cowsтАЭ reprises 21bc v─Б╠Бjebhiс╕е тАж g├│madbhiс╕е and is then echoed by vraj├бс╣Г g├│mantam тАЬenclosure of cowsтАЭ in 24ab.

English translation:

тАЬThen the desroyer of the Dasyus, proceeds to the cattl-crowded folds of Kuvitsa, and by his acts opens them for us.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Kuvitsa, a person n who does much (kuvit) harm (syati)

Jamison Brereton

For the smiter of Dasyus will certainly go forth to somebodyтАЩs cattle enclosure;
with his powers he will open it up.

Jamison Brereton Notes

There is some difference of opinion on the source of the apparent indefinite kuv├нtsa-, a hapax. Geldner (n. 24a) asserts that sasya is the gen. corresponding to s├бsmin, enclitic after kuv├нd (presumably presupposing a notional word space kuv├нt sasya). But the standard opinion, already registered by Grassmann (тЖР BR; see also explicitly AiG II.1.327, repeated AiG II.2.924), is that it is derived from the univerbation of a syntactic sequence kuv├нt s├б (roughly тАЬis it indeed this one?тАЭ), which is then secondarily inflected. This seems the more likely explanation, and in fact there is such a sequence attested in IV.51.4 kuv├нt s├б. This passage contains a deliberative either/or question тАЬshould it be the old course or a new one тАж?тАЭ kuv├нt s├б тАж san├бyo n├бvo v─Б y─Б╠Бmaс╕е, a context that favors development into an indefinite of the type тАЬsomeone or other.тАЭ In fact, our passage might be more clearly rendered as тАЬto the cattle enclosure of someone or other.тАЭ

To which the Dasyu-slayer goes.

Partnership with you is difficult to attain. You are, o hero, the cow for him who seeks cattle.

тАЬDelight your person n with the libation (offered) for the sake of treasure; subject not your worshipper to his reviler.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Find exhilaration from the stalk, then, to show great generosity with your own person.
You will not put your praiser to scorn.

English translation:

тАЬThese our praises tend, as the libationsa are repeatedly poured out, eagerly to you who are gratified by praise, as the milch kine (hasten) to their calves.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

These songs come near to you at every pressing, o you who long for songs,
as milk-cows do their calfтАФ

Jamison Brereton Notes

Although, as just noted, thereтАЩs no unity in the tс╣Ыca, there is some continuity between tс╣Ыcas. Like the first vs. of the previous tс╣Ыca (25), this one has polarized nom. #im─Б╠Бс╕е тАж g├нraс╕е# тАЬthese songsтАЭ framing the first hemistich, which responds to the acc. g├нraс╕е in the middle of the tс╣Ыca before that (23c). Moreover, the simile тАЬlike cows their calfтАЭ (28c) reprises тАЬlike mothers their calfтАЭ in 25c.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay the praises of many worshippers offered at the sacrifice, (accompanied) by (sacrificial) viands, invigorate you, destroyer of multitudes.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

At the sacrifice: viv─Бci, at the sacrifice called Vivac, because various praises and prayers are hen repeated

Jamison Brereton

(You,) the first among many at the verbal contest of the many
praiser-singers,
who compete for the prize with their prizes.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. is syntactically dependent on 28, with the acc. pur┼лt├бmam picking up tv─Б in 28a.

The cognate expression v─Б╠Бjebhir v─Бjayat─Б╠Бm тАЬcompeting for the prize with their prizesтАЭ is a bit puzzling. I interpr. it as being a slight play on words, with the instr. v─Б╠Бjebhiс╕е referring to the singersтАЩ songs, expressing the means by which they compete, while the prizes they compete for are material goods and fame. This interpr. is somewhat supported by the next vs., where we hope that our praise-song is the most successful one.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Again no unity in the tс╣Ыca.

Griffith

To thee most oft invoked, amid the many singers’ rivalry
Who beg with all their might for wealth.

Geldner

Zu ihm, dem Ersten unter Vielen im Wettstreit der vielen S├дnger, die um die Siegerpreise wetteifern.

Grassmann

Dem reichsten unter vielen dir im Wettgesang der Preisenden, Die reich an allen Gaben sind.

English translation:

тАЬMay our most elevating praise be near, Indra, to you, and urge us to (the acquisition of) great riches.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Most elevating praise: stomo v─Бhiс╣гс╣нhaс╕е = voс╕Нhс╣Ыtama, most bearing, uplifting, elevating

Jamison Brereton

Let ours be the praise song that best conveys you nearest, Indra. Impel us toward great wealth.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Notice the very un-─Аrya phonology of the name of the patron, Bс╣Ыbu with two plain bтАЩs. (On Bс╣Ыbu as patron see Kuiper, Aryans, p. 6.) It is probably not an accident that this vs. contains only one of two reff. to the Gaс╣Еg─Б in the RV (the other a voc. gaс╣Еge in X.75.5), since the Gaс╣Еg─Б is at the limits of the RVic geographical horizon.

The simile is more lit. тАЬ(he is) broad like the Gangetic girth.тАЭ

English translation:

тАЬBс╣Ыbu presided over the high plural ces of the Paс╣Зis, like the elevated bank of the Ganges.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Bс╣Ыbu paс╣З─лn─Бm varс╣гiс╣гс╣нhe m┼лrdhan adhyasth─Бt = he stood over upon the high plural ce, as if it were on the forehead of the Paс╣Зis; m┼лrdhavat ucchrite sthale; the Paс╣Зis may be either merchants or traders, or asuras, so termed; like the elevated bank of the Ganges: uruс╕е kakс╣гo na g─Бс╣Еgyaс╕е = gaс╣Еg─Бy─Бс╕е kule vist─лrс╣Зe iv─Б, as on the broad bank of the Ganges, that is, as the bank is above the bed of the river.

Jamison Brereton

Br╠еbu has stood upon the highest head of the niggards [/Paс╣Зis];
(he is) as broad of girth as the GangesтАФ

P─Бdas ab are identical to VIII.94.3. For my interpr. of the hemistich and esp. of the phrase ary├б ─Б╠Бsee comm. there. Given the un-─Аrya phonology of Bс╣ЫbuтАЩs name, there may be a particular pleasure in hymning the un-─Аrya patron Bс╣Ыbu away from the ar├нVI.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬOf whom, prompt as the wind, the liberal donation of thousands (of cattle) has been quickly given to (me) soliciting a gift.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

(He) whose propitious gift in the thousands, at a speed like the windтАЩs, is ready for giving all at once.

Griffith

He whose good bounty, thousandfold, swift as the rushing of the wind,
Suddenly offers as a gift.

Geldner

Dessen Freigebigkeit, rasch wie die des Vayu gl├╝ckbringend, tausendbringend, sogleich zu schenken bereitwillig ist.

Grassmann

Er, dessen tausendfache Gabe wie im Fluge des Windes sogleich zum Lohne geschenkt wird.

English translation:

тАЬWhom, therefore, we all, who are the profferers and bestowers of praise ever commend, as the pious Bс╣Ыbu, the donor of thousands (of cattle), the receiver of thousands (of laudations).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Bс╣Ыbu is called Takс╣г─Б the carpenter or artificer of the Paс╣Зis; the legend is preserved by Manu (10.107) and N─лti Ma├▒jar─л: the illustrious Bharadv─Бja, with his son, distressed by hunger in a lonely forest, accepted many cows from the carpenter Bс╣Ыbu; the с╣Ыca is attributed to Sayu, the son of Bharadv─Бja; j─Бtito hino api d─Бtс╣Ыtv─Бt sarvatra ┼Ыreс╣гс╣нho bhavati, a person n inferior by caste becomes everywhere distinguished by genitive rosity

Jamison Brereton

So then do all our bards always hymn here, away from (the sacrifice) of the stranger,
Br╠еbu, the best giver of thousands, the patron, the best winner of
thousands.

Griffith

So all our singers ever praise the pious Brbu’s noble deed,
Chief, best to give his thousands, best to give a thousand liberal gifts.

Geldner

Das sollen von uns fein alle, auch die hohen Herren wissen: Immerdar preisen die Dichter den Bribu, den gr├╢├Яten Tausendschenker, den freigebigen Herren, den gr├╢├Яten Tausendspender.

Grassmann

Darum r├╝hmen stets alle unsre treuen S├дnger den Bribu, der am meisten schenkt, den F├╝rsten, der am meisten schenkt.

Elizarenkova
